Use this function only when\nyou've derived a new value from a sensitive value in a way that eliminates the\nsensitive portions of the value.\n\nNormally Terraform tracks when you use expressions to derive a new value from\na value that is marked as sensitive, so that the result can also be marked\nas sensitive.\n\nHowever, you may wish to write expressions that derive non-sensitive results\nfrom sensitive values. For example, if you know based on details of your\nparticular system and its threat model that a SHA256 hash of a particular\nsensitive value is safe to include clearly in Terraform output, you could use\nthe `nonsensitive` function to indicate that, overriding Terraform's normal\nconservative behavior:\n\n```hcl\noutput \"sensitive_example_hash\" {\n  value = nonsensitive(sha256(var.sensitive_example))\n}\n```\n\nAnother example might be if the original value is only partially sensitive and\nyou've written expressions to separate the sensitive and non-sensitive parts:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"mixed_content_json\" {\n  description = \"A JSON string containing a mixture of sensitive and non-sensitive values.\"\n  type        = string\n  sensitive   = true\n}\n\nlocals {\n  # mixed_content is derived from var.mixed_content_json, so it\n  # is also considered to be sensitive.\n  mixed_content = jsondecode(var.mixed_content_json)\n\n  # password_from_json is derived from mixed_content, so it's\n  # also considered to be sensitive.\n  password_from_json = local.mixed_content[\"password\"]\n\n  # username_from_json would normally be considered to be\n  # sensitive too, but system-specific knowledge tells us\n  # that the username is a non-sensitive fragment of the\n  # original document, and so we can override Terraform's\n  # determination.\n  username_from_json = nonsensitive(local.mixed_content[\"username\"])\n}\n```\n\nWhen you use this function, it's your responsibility to ensure that the\nexpression passed as its argument will remove all sensitive content from\nthe sensitive value it depends on. By passing a value to `nonsensitive` you are\ndeclaring to Terraform that you have done all that is necessary to ensure that\nthe resulting value has no sensitive content, even though it was derived\nfrom sensitive content. If a sensitive value appears in Terraform's output\ndue to an inappropriate call to `nonsensitive` in your module, that's a bug in\nyour module and not a bug in Terraform itself.\n**Use this function sparingly and only with due care.**\n\n`nonsensitive` will make no changes to values that aren't marked as sensitive, even though such a call may be redundant and potentially confusing.\nUse `nonsensitive` only after careful consideration and with definite intent.\n\nConsider including a comment adjacent to your call to explain to future\nmaintainers what makes the usage safe and thus what invariants they must take\ncare to preserve under future modifications.\n\n## Examples\n\nThe following examples are from `terraform console` when running in the\ncontext of the example above with `variable \"mixed_content_json\"` and\nthe local value `mixed_content`, with a valid JSON string assigned to\n`var.mixed_content_json`.\n\n```\n> var.mixed_content_json\n(sensitive value)\n> local.mixed_content\n(sensitive value)\n> local.mixed_content[\"password\"]\n(sensitive value)\n> nonsensitive(local.mixed_content[\"username\"])\n\"zqb\"\n> nonsensitive(\"clear\")\n\nError: Invalid function argument\n\nInvalid value for \"value\" parameter: the given value is not sensitive, so this\ncall is redundant.\n```\n\nNote though that it's always your responsibility to use `nonsensitive` only\nwhen it's safe to do so. If you use `nonsensitive` with content that\n_ought to be_ considered sensitive then that content will be disclosed:\n\n```\n> nonsensitive(var.mixed_content_json)\n<<EOT\n{\n  \"username\": \"zqb\",\n  \"password\": \"p4ssw0rd\"\n}\nEOT\n> nonsensitive(local.mixed_content)\n{\n  \"password\" = \"p4ssw0rd\"\n  \"username\" = \"zqb\"\n}\n> nonsensitive(local.mixed_content[\"password\"])\n\"p4ssw0rd\"\n```\n---\npage_title: issensitive - Functions - Configuration Language\ndescription: The issensitive function true if the value passed is marked as sensitive\n---\n\n# `issensitive` Function\n\n-> **Note:** This function is only available in Terraform v1.8 and later.\n\n`issensitive` takes any value and returns true if Terraform\ntreats it as sensitive, with the same meaning and behavior as for\n[sensitive input variables](/terraform/language/values/variables#suppressing-values-in-cli-output).\n\nIf a value not marked as sensitive is passed the function returns false.\n\nSee [`sensitive`](/terraform/language/functions/sensitive), [`nonsensitive`](/terraform/language/functions/nonsensitive), and [sensitive input variables](/terraform/language/values/variables#suppressing-values-in-cli-output) for more information on sensitive values.\n\n## Examples\n\n```\n> issensitive(sensitive(\"secret\"))\ntrue\n> issensitive(\"hello\")\nfalse\n> sensitive(var.my-var-with-sensitive-set-to-true)\ntrue\n```"
}

The workflows of `ephemeralasnull` are subject to change.\n\n\nThis topic provides reference information about the `ephemeralasnull` function. The `ephemeralasnull` function accepts an ephemeral value and returns `null`. \n\n## Introduction\n\nYou can use the `ephemeralasnull` function to nullify ephemeral values. For example, if you pass an object with a nested ephemeral value to `ephemeralasnull`,it nullifies any ephemeral values within that object.\n\n## Syntax\n\nUse the `ephemeralasnull` function with the following syntax:\n\n```hcl\nephemeralasnull(var.my_ephemeral_value)\n```\n\nIn the following example, you can pass the `ephemeralasnull` function an ephemeral value, and the function returns `null`:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"example\" {\n  type      = string\n  default   = \"test\"\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\n# This output returns null.\noutput \"example_output\" {\n  value       = ephemeralasnull(var.example)\n}\n```\n\nFor more information on which Terraform blocks can be ephemeral, refer to ephemeral [inputs](/terraform/language/values/variables#exclude-values-from-state), [outputs](/terraform/language/values/outputs#ephemeral-avoid-storing-values-in-state-or-plan-files), and [resources](/terraform/language/resources/ephemeral).\n\n## Example use case\n\nThe following example shows how you can use the  `ephemeralasnull` function to intake a map that contains some ephemeral values, and output the values that are not ephemeral.\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"session_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  default   = \"test\"\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\nvariable \"configuration\" {\n  type = map(string)\n  default = {\n    \"env\" = \"development\"\n  }\n}\n\n# This is a contrived example, but this pattern works with any object that is a mix of ephemeral and non-ephemeral values. \nlocals {\n  configuration_with_token = merge(\n    var.configuration,\n    { \"session_token\" = var.session_token }\n  )\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\noutput \"configuration_settings\" {\n# Using ephemeralasnull enables you to output the non-ephemeral values.\n  value       = ephemeralasnull(local.things_with_token)\n  description = \"Environment setting.\"\n}\n```\n\nWhen you apply the above configuration, Terraform returns the `ephemeral` values in `locals.configuration_settings` as `null`. This lets you output the non-ephemeral value `env`.\n\n```hcl\nOutputs:\n\nconfiguration_settings = {\n  \"env\" = \"development\"\n  \"session_token\" = tostring(null)\n}\n```"

  "stdout": "-> **Note**: Ephemeral local values are in public beta and available in Terraform v1.10 and later. The workflows of ephemeral locals are subject to change.\n\nLocal values implicitly become ephemeral if you reference an ephemeral value when you assign that local a value. For example, you can create a local that references an ephemeral `service_token`.\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"service_name\" {\n  type    = string\n  default = \"forum\"\n}\n\nvariable \"environment\" {\n  type    = string\n  default = \"dev\"\n}\n\nvariable \"service_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\nlocals {\n  service_tag   = \"${var.service_name}-${var.environment}\"\n  session_token = \"${var.service_name}:${var.service_token}\"\n}\n```\n\nThe `local.session_token` value is implicitly ephemeral because it relies on an ephemeral variable.\n\n## Using Local Values\n\nOnce a local value is declared, you can reference it in\n[expressions](/terraform/language/expressions) as `local.<NAME>`.\n\n-> **Note:** Local values are _created_ by a `locals` block (plural), but you\n_reference_ them as attributes on an object named `local` (singular). Make sure\nto leave off the \"s\" when referencing a local value!\n\n```hcl\nresource \"aws_instance\" \"example\" {\n  # ...\n\n  tags = local.common_tags\n}\n```\n\nA local value can only be accessed in expressions within the module where it\nwas declared.\n\n## When To Use Local Values\n\nLocal values can be helpful to avoid repeating the same values or expressions\nmultiple times in a configuration, but if overused they can also make a\nconfiguration hard to read by future maintainers by hiding the actual values\nused.\n\nUse local values only in moderation, in situations where a single value or\nresult is used in many places _and_ that value is likely to be changed in"
}

  "stdout": "## 1.10.0 (November 27, 2024)\n\nNEW FEATURES:\n - **Ephemeral resources**: Ephemeral resources are read anew during each phase of Terraform evaluation, and cannot be persisted to state storage. Ephemeral resources always produce ephemeral values.\n - **Ephemeral values**: Input variables and outputs can now be defined as ephemeral. Ephemeral values may only be used in certain contexts in Terraform configuration, and are not persisted to the plan or state files.\n    - **`ephemeralasnull` function**: a function takes a value of any type and returns a similar value of the same type with any ephemeral values replaced with non-ephemeral null values and all non-ephemeral values preserved.\n\nBUG FIXES:\n\n- The `secret_suffix` in the `kubernetes` backend now includes validation to prevent errors when the `secret_suffix` ends with a number ([#35666](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35666)).\n- The error message for an invalid default value for an input variable now indicates when the problem is with a nested value in a complex data type. ([#35465](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35465))\n- Sensitive marks could be incorrectly transferred to nested resource values, causing erroneous changes during a plan ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\n- Allow unknown `error_message` values to pass the core validate step, so variable validation can be completed later during plan\n  ([#35537](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35537))\n- Unencoded slashes within GitHub module source refs were being truncated and incorrectly used as subdirectories in the request path ([#35552](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35552))\n- Terraform refresh-only plans with output only changes are now applyable. ([#35812](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35812))\n- Postconditions referencing `self` with many instances could encounter an error during evaluation ([#35895](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35895))\n- The `plantimestamp()` function would return an invalid date during validation ([#35902](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35902))\n- Updates to resources which were forced to use create_before_destroy could lose that flag in the state temporarily and cause cycles if immediately removed from the configuration ([#35966](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35966))\n- backend/cloud: Prefer KV tags, even when tags are defined as set ([#35937](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35937))\n- Simplify config generation (`plan -generate-config-out`) for string attributes that contain primitive types (e.g. numbers or booleans) ([#35984](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35984))\n- config: `issensitive` could incorrectly assert that an unknown value was not sensitive during plan, but later became sensitive during apply, causing failures where changes did not match the planned result ([#36012](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36012))\n- config: The evaluation of conditional expressions and for expression in HCL could lose marks with certain combinations of unknown values ([#36017](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36017))\n\nENHANCEMENTS:\n\n- The `element` function now accepts negative indices ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\n- Import block validation has been improved to provide more useful errors and catch more invalid cases during `terraform validate` ([#35543](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35543))\n- Performance enhancements for resource evaluation, especially when large numbers of resource instances are involved ([#35558](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35558))\n- The `plan`, `apply`, and `refresh` commands now produce a deprecated warning when using the `-state` flag. Instead use the `path` attribute within the `local` backend to modify the state file. ([#35660](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35660))\n- backend/cos: Add new auth for Tencent Cloud backend ([#35888](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35888))\n\nUPGRADE NOTES:\n\n- backend/s3: Removes deprecated attributes for assuming IAM role. Must use the `assume_role` block ([#35721](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35721))\n- backend/s3: The s3 backend now supports S3 native state locking. When used with DynamoDB-based locking, locks will be acquired from both sources. In a future minor release of Terraform the DynamoDB locking mechanism and associated arguments will be deprecated. ([#35661](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35661))\n- `moved`: Moved blocks now respect reserved keywords when parsing resource addresses. Configurations that reference resources with type names that match top level blocks and keywords from `moved` blocks will need to prepend the `resource.` identifier to these references. ([#35850](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35850))\n- config: In order to ensure consistency in results from HCL conditional expressions, marks must be combined from all values within the expression to avoid losing mark information. This typically improves accuracy when validating configuration, but users may see sensitive results where they were lost previously.\n\n## Previous Releases\n\nFor information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\n\n- [v1.9](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.9/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.8](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.8/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.7](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.7/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.6](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.6/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.5](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.5/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.4](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.4/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.3](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.3/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.2](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.2/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.1](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.1/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v1.0](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.0/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.15](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.15/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.14/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.13/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.12/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [v0.11 and earlier](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.11/CHANGELOG.md)"

119. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 was released on November 27, 2024. It is a minor release in the stable Terraform v1.0 series and honors the [Terraform v1.0 Compatibility Promises](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1-compatibility-promises).\n\nThis release introduces several breaking changes and significant new features:\n\n- **Breaking**: Removed deprecated root-level IAM role assumption attributes from the S3 backend \u2014 must migrate to `assume_role` block syntax\n- **Breaking**: `moved` blocks now enforce reserved keyword restrictions on resource type names \u2014 may require adding `resource.` prefix\n- **Behavioral change**: Conditional expressions now preserve sensitive marks in all branches \u2014 previously some marks were silently dropped\n- **New feature**: Ephemeral resources, ephemeral input variables, and ephemeral outputs \u2014 a mechanism to avoid persisting sensitive values to state\n- **New feature**: S3 native state locking (`use_lockfile`) as an experimental opt-in alternative to DynamoDB locking\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend: Removal of Deprecated Root-Level IAM Role Assumption Attributes\n\n#### What Changed and Why\n\nIn v1.9.0, the following root-level attributes in the S3 backend were deprecated with replacements inside an `assume_role` block. In **v1.10.0, these deprecated attributes have been completely removed**. Any S3 backend configuration still using them will fail with an error at `terraform init`.\n\n| Removed Attribute | Replacement Inside `assume_role` Block |\n|---|---|\n| `role_arn` | `assume_role.role_arn` |\n| `session_name` | `assume_role.session_name` |\n| `external_id` | `assume_role.external_id` |\n| `assume_role_duration_seconds` | `assume_role.duration` |\n| `assume_role_policy` | `assume_role.policy` |\n| `assume_role_policy_arns` | `assume_role.policy_arns` |\n| `assume_role_tags` | `assume_role.tags` |\n| `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` | `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys` |\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0 \u2014 deprecated but functional)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket       = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key          = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region       = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # These root-level attributes are REMOVED in v1.10.0\n    role_arn                     = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n    session_name                 = \"terraform-session\"\n    external_id                  = \"my-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds = 3600\n    assume_role_policy           = jsonencode({ ... })\n    assume_role_policy_arns      = [\"arn:aws:iam::aws:policy/ReadOnlyAccess\"]\n    assume_role_tags = {\n      Environment = \"production\"\n    }\n    assume_role_transitive_tag_keys = [\"Environment\"]\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0 \u2014 required syntax)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    assume_role = {\n      role_arn     = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n      session_name = \"terraform-session\"\n      external_id  = \"my-external-id\"\n      duration     = \"1h\"\n      policy       = jsonencode({ ... })\n      policy_arns  = [\"arn:aws:iam::aws:policy/ReadOnlyAccess\"]\n      tags = {\n        Environment = \"production\"\n      }\n      transitive_tag_keys = [\"Environment\"]\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Step-by-Step Migration Instructions\n\n1. **Audit all S3 backend configurations** \u2014 search your codebase for `backend \"s3\"` blocks and identify any that use the root-level deprecated attributes:\n\n   ```bash\n   grep -rn \"role_arn\\|session_name\\|external_id\\|assume_role_duration_seconds\\|assume_role_policy\\|assume_role_tags\\|assume_role_transitive_tag_keys\" \\\n     --include=\"*.tf\" --include=\"*.tfvars\" .\n   ```\n\n   Also check any partial backend configuration files (commonly passed with `-backend-config`).\n\n2. **Refactor each backend block** \u2014 move all role assumption attributes inside an `assume_role = { ... }` block:\n\n   - `role_arn` \u2192 `assume_role.role_arn` (note: now **required** within the block if assuming a role)\n   - `session_name` \u2192 `assume_role.session_name`\n   - `external_id` \u2192 `assume_role.external_id`\n   - `assume_role_duration_seconds` (integer, seconds) \u2192 `assume_role.duration` (string, e.g., `\"1h30m\"`)\n   - `assume_role_policy` \u2192 `assume_role.policy`\n   - `assume_role_policy_arns` \u2192 `assume_role.policy_arns`\n   - `assume_role_tags` \u2192 `assume_role.tags`\n   - `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` \u2192 `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys`\n\n   > **Note on `duration` format**: The old `assume_role_duration_seconds` accepted an integer (e.g., `3600`). The new `assume_role.duration` accepts a duration string (e.g., `\"1h\"`, `\"90m\"`, `\"1h30m\"`). Valid range is 15 minutes (`15m`) to 12 hours (`12h`).\n\n3. **Run `terraform init`** on each updated backend configuration to validate the new syntax.\n\n4. **Check partial backend config files** \u2014 if you use `-backend-config=backend.hcl` or `-backend-config=\"key=value\"` flags, update those as well.\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- The `assume_role` value is a **block** (or map), not a string. Use `assume_role = { ... }`, not `assume_role = \"...\"`.\n- If you only used `role_arn` at the root level, you now need `assume_role = { role_arn = \"...\" }`.\n- Multiple `assume_role` blocks are supported \u2014 roles are assumed in order \u2014 but this was not available with the old root-level attributes.\n- The `duration` format changed from seconds (integer) to a duration string. `3600` seconds becomes `\"1h\"`.\n\n---\n\n### 2. S3 Backend: New S3 Native State Locking\n\n#### What Changed and Why\n\nThe S3 backend gained a new experimental opt-in feature: **S3-native state locking** using `.tflock` files. This is not a breaking change by itself since it is opt-in, but it has operational implications worth understanding before upgrading.\n\nWhen `use_lockfile = true` is set, Terraform creates a lock file alongside the state file in S3 (same path, with a `.tflock` extension). When both `use_lockfile` and `dynamodb_table` are configured, **both locking mechanisms must succeed** before operations proceed.\n\n> **Important**: In a future minor version of Terraform, the DynamoDB locking mechanism and its associated arguments will be deprecated. The `use_lockfile` attribute will move out of experimental status at that time.\n\n#### Enabling S3 Native Locking (Optional)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket       = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key          = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region       = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Opt-in to experimental S3-native locking\n    use_lockfile = true\n\n    # Can be used alongside DynamoDB locking (both must succeed)\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-state-locks\"\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### IAM Permission Updates Required\n\nIf you enable `use_lockfile = true`, ensure the IAM principal running Terraform has permissions to read, write, and delete the lock file in S3:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n  \"Statement\": [\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Action\": [\"s3:GetObject\", \"s3:PutObject\", \"s3:DeleteObject\"],\n      \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-bucket/path/to/state.tflock\"\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\nFor workspace-aware configurations, the lock file path follows the workspace state path pattern with `.tflock` appended.\n\n---\n\n### 3. `moved` Blocks: Reserved Keyword Restriction on Resource Type Names\n\n#### What Changed and Why\n\nIn v1.10.0, `moved` block resource address parsing now **rejects resource type names that conflict with reserved keywords** (`local`, `each`, `self`, `count`, `module`, `path`, `terraform`, `var`, and other top-level block types).\n\nPreviously, a `moved` block referencing a resource whose type name happened to match a keyword (e.g., `resource \"local\" \"my_file\" { ... }`) would be parsed without error but could produce incorrect behavior. Now Terraform will report an error and require you to prepend `resource.` to the address to disambiguate.\n\n#### Affected Configurations\n\nThis affects `moved` blocks where the resource type name collides with a Terraform keyword or top-level block type. Common examples include:\n\n- `local` (conflicts with `local` values)\n- `count` (conflicts with `count` meta-argument)\n- `each` (conflicts with `each` in for_each)\n- `self` (conflicts with `self` reference)\n- `module` (conflicts with `module` block)\n- `var` (conflicts with `var` reference)\n- `path` (conflicts with `path` object)\n- `terraform` (conflicts with `terraform` block)\n- `data` (conflicts with `data` sources)\n- `check` (conflicts with `check` block)\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0 \u2014 ambiguous but accepted)\n\n```hcl\n# Resource with a type name matching a keyword\nresource \"local\" \"config\" {\n  filename = \"/tmp/config.txt\"\n  content  = \"hello\"\n}\n\n# Old moved block \u2014 ambiguous in v1.9.0, error in v1.10.0\nmoved {\n  from = local.config\n  to   = local.config_v2\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0 \u2014 required syntax)\n\n```hcl\nresource \"local\" \"config\" {\n  filename = \"/tmp/config.txt\"\n  content  = \"hello\"\n}\n\n# Explicit resource. prefix required when type name conflicts with keywords\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.config\n  to   = resource.local.config_v2\n}\n```\n\n#### Step-by-Step Migration Instructions\n\n1. **Find all `moved` blocks** in your configuration:\n\n   ```bash\n   grep -rn \"^moved {\" --include=\"*.tf\" .\n   ```\n\n2. **Check both `from` and `to` addresses** in each `moved` block. For each address, identify whether the first component (the resource type name) matches any of the following reserved keywords:\n\n   `local`, `each`, `self`, `count`, `module`, `var`, `path`, `terraform`, `data`, `check`, `resource`\n\n3. **Add the `resource.` prefix** to any address where the resource type name conflicts with a keyword:\n\n   ```hcl\n   # BEFORE\n   moved {\n     from = local.old_name\n     to   = local.new_name\n   }\n\n   # AFTER\n   moved {\n     from = resource.local.old_name\n     to   = resource.local.new_name\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Run `terraform validate`** to confirm no moved block errors remain.\n\n5. **Run `terraform plan`** to verify the moved blocks are interpreted correctly (the plan should show moves, not destroys+creates).\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- Only addresses in `moved` blocks are affected. Normal resource references (in `resource`, `data`, `locals`, etc.) are unaffected.\n- The `resource.` prefix is only required when the type name **conflicts with a keyword**. Resources with ordinary type names (e.g., `aws_instance`, `azurerm_resource_group`) do not require the prefix.\n- Both `from` and `to` addresses may independently require the prefix \u2014 check both.\n- If you have modules with `moved` blocks, the inner module addresses also need to be checked.\n\n---\n\n## Behavioral Changes\n\n### 4. Sensitive Value Handling in Conditional Expressions\n\n#### What Changed and Why\n\nIn v1.10.0, a bug was fixed in how HCL evaluates conditional expressions and `for` expressions: **sensitive marks (and other value marks) are now consistently propagated across all branches** of an expression, even when some branches contain unknown values.\n\nPreviously, certain combinations of unknown values in conditional expressions could cause marks to be silently dropped. This meant a value that should have been treated as sensitive was not, potentially exposing it in plan output or in state without warning.\n\nThe fix ensures that if any value in a conditional expression (condition, true branch, or false branch) carries a sensitive mark, that mark is preserved in the result. This is more correct behavior and improves security, but it means **configurations that previously produced non-sensitive outputs may now produce sensitive outputs**.\n\nAdditionally, the `issensitive()` function could previously incorrectly assert that an unknown value was not sensitive during plan, but later become sensitive during apply, causing plan/apply mismatches. This has also been fixed.\n\n#### Scenarios Where You May See Changes\n\n**Scenario 1: Conditional with a sensitive condition**\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"secret\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\n# In v1.9.0: this may produce a non-sensitive value in some cases\n# In v1.10.0: result is always sensitive because secret is sensitive\noutput \"result\" {\n  value = var.secret == \"expected\" ? \"yes\" : \"no\"\n}\n```\n\n**Scenario 2: Conditional with a sensitive branch value**\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"use_secret\" {\n  type    = bool\n  default = false\n}\n\nvariable \"secret_value\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\n# In v1.9.0: if use_secret is unknown at plan time, marks could be lost\n# In v1.10.0: result is always sensitive because secret_value is sensitive\noutput \"chosen_value\" {\n  value = var.use_secret ? var.secret_value : \"public-default\"\n}\n```\n\n**Scenario 3: For expression with sensitive values**\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"secrets\" {\n  type      = list(string)\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\n# In v1.10.0: transformed values retain the sensitive mark\nlocals {\n  processed = [for s in var.secrets : upper(s)]\n}\n```\n\n#### Impact Assessment\n\nThis change **does not alter the underlying values** \u2014 it only changes whether Terraform marks them as sensitive. The practical effects are:\n\n- Plan output may now show `(sensitive value)` where it previously showed the actual value\n- Outputs that previously appeared in the output table may now be suppressed as sensitive\n- `issensitive()` function results will be more accurate (fewer false negatives during plan)\n\n#### How to Use `nonsensitive()` to Override When Needed\n\nIf you have a derivation from a sensitive value that you know is safe to expose (because the sensitive information has been removed in the transformation), you can use the `nonsensitive()` function to explicitly override Terraform's conservative behavior:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\n# This is derived from a sensitive value but only shows length \u2014 safe to expose\noutput \"password_length\" {\n  # nonsensitive() tells Terraform this derived value is not sensitive\n  value = nonsensitive(length(var.db_password))\n}\n\n# A hash of a password \u2014 whether this is safe depends on your threat model\noutput \"password_hash\" {\n  value = nonsensitive(sha256(var.db_password))\n}\n```\n\n> **Warning**: Only use `nonsensitive()` when you are certain the derived value does not expose sensitive information. Using it incorrectly will cause sensitive data to appear in plain text in Terraform output and state files. Add a comment explaining why the usage is safe.\n\n#### Step-by-Step Migration Instructions\n\n1. **Run `terraform plan`** after upgrading to identify any new sensitive value warnings or output changes.\n\n2. **Review outputs** that previously showed plain values but now show `(sensitive value)`. Determine whether:\n   - The output _should_ be sensitive (in which case no action is needed \u2014 this is a security improvement), or\n   - The output genuinely does not contain sensitive information (in which case use `nonsensitive()`)\n\n3. **Update CI/CD pipelines** that parse plan output \u2014 if your automation reads specific output values from `terraform output`, ensure it handles `(sensitive value)` appropriately.\n\n4. **Review `issensitive()` usage** \u2014 if you used `issensitive()` in validation conditions or locals to conditionally handle values, test that the corrected behavior meets your expectations.\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- Do not add `nonsensitive()` indiscriminately to silence warnings. Each usage requires careful consideration of whether it is actually safe.\n- The change improves correctness \u2014 if you were relying on marks being dropped (e.g., to output a sensitive value without marking it), that was a bug and you should redesign that part of your configuration.\n- `sensitive` and `ephemeral` are separate concepts \u2014 `sensitive` controls display and state storage, while `ephemeral` (new in v1.10.0) prevents state storage entirely. See the Ephemeral Values section for details.\n\n---\n\n## New Features with Migration Impact\n\n### 5. Ephemeral Resources and Values\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces a new concept of **ephemeral values**: data that is available during Terraform operations but is **never written to state or plan files**. This is a fundamentally different mechanism from `sensitive`, which only suppresses display of values that are still stored in state.\n\n> **Note**: Ephemeral resources, variables, and outputs are in public beta in v1.10.0. Workflows may change in future versions.\n\n#### Ephemeral Resources\n\nA new `ephemeral` block type defines resources that are read fresh during each operation phase and never stored in state:\n\n```hcl\nephemeral \"aws_secretsmanager_secret_version\" \"db_creds\" {\n  secret_id = data.aws_db_instance.example.master_user_secret[0].secret_arn\n}\n\nlocals {\n  credentials = jsondecode(ephemeral.aws_secretsmanager_secret_version.db_creds.secret_string)\n}\n\nprovider \"postgresql\" {\n  host     = data.aws_db_instance.example.address\n  username = local.credentials[\"username\"]\n  password = local.credentials[\"password\"]\n}\n```\n\n**Ephemeral resource lifecycle:**\n1. **Open**: Terraform fetches the resource (e.g., obtains a Vault lease)\n2. **Renew** (if needed): Terraform keeps the resource alive if the operation is long-running\n3. **Close**: Terraform releases the resource when it is no longer needed (e.g., ends the Vault lease)\n\n**Supported meta-arguments for ephemeral resources:**\n- `depends_on`\n- `count`\n- `for_each`\n- `provider`\n- `lifecycle`\n\n**Not supported:** `provisioner` meta-argument.\n\n#### Ephemeral Input Variables\n\nInput variables can be marked as ephemeral to prevent their values from being written to state or plan files:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"session_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n```\n\nUnlike `sensitive`, which still stores values in state (just marking them as sensitive), `ephemeral = true` means the value is **never persisted**. This is appropriate for short-lived tokens, one-time passwords, or credentials that rotate frequently.\n\n**Valid contexts for ephemeral variables:**\n- Other ephemeral variables\n- Local values (which become implicitly ephemeral)\n- Ephemeral resources\n- Ephemeral outputs\n- Provider configuration blocks\n- `provisioner` and `connection` blocks\n\n#### Ephemeral Outputs\n\nOutputs in child modules can be marked ephemeral to pass ephemeral values between modules without persisting them:\n\n```hcl\n# modules/secrets/main.tf\noutput \"api_key\" {\n  value       = ephemeral.vault_kv_secret.app.data[\"api_key\"]\n  ephemeral   = true\n  description = \"Temporary API key for the application.\"\n}\n```\n\n> **Restriction**: Ephemeral outputs cannot be set in the **root module**. They are only supported in child modules.\n\n#### The `ephemeralasnull` Function\n\nA new built-in function `ephemeralasnull` converts ephemeral values to `null`, enabling outputs of mixed ephemeral/non-ephemeral objects:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"session_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\nvariable \"environment\" {\n  type    = string\n  default = \"production\"\n}\n\nlocals {\n  config = {\n    env   = var.environment\n    token = var.session_token\n  }\n  # implicitly ephemeral because it contains an ephemeral value\n}\n\noutput \"config_summary\" {\n  # ephemeralasnull replaces ephemeral values with null,\n  # allowing non-ephemeral values to be output\n  value = ephemeralasnull(local.config)\n}\n# Output: { \"env\" = \"production\", \"token\" = null }\n```\n\n#### Migrating from `sensitive` to `ephemeral` for Secret Handling\n\nIf your current configurations use `sensitive` purely to prevent secrets from appearing in state, consider migrating to `ephemeral` for stronger guarantees:\n\n| Mechanism | Appears in State | Displayed in UI | Use Case |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `sensitive = true` | Yes (encrypted at rest if backend supports it) | Suppressed | Data that must be preserved across runs |\n| `ephemeral = true` | **No** | Not displayed | Temporary credentials, tokens, one-time values |\n\n**Before (v1.9.0 and earlier \u2014 sensitive approach):**\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nresource \"aws_db_instance\" \"main\" {\n  password = var.db_password\n  # password is stored in state (sensitive but present)\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0 \u2014 ephemeral approach for maximum privacy):**\n\n```hcl\nephemeral \"aws_secretsmanager_secret_version\" \"db_pass\" {\n  secret_id = aws_secretsmanager_secret.db_password.id\n}\n\nresource \"aws_db_instance\" \"main\" {\n  password = ephemeral.aws_secretsmanager_secret_version.db_pass.secret_string\n  # password is never written to state\n}\n```\n\n> **Note**: Not all resource arguments accept ephemeral values. Provider support is required. Check the relevant provider's documentation for which arguments support ephemeral values.\n\n#### Implicit Ephemeral Propagation\n\nEphemeral values propagate implicitly through local values and expressions:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"api_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\nlocals {\n  # Implicitly ephemeral \u2014 inherits from var.api_token\n  auth_header = \"Bearer ${var.api_token}\"\n\n  # Not ephemeral \u2014 does not reference ephemeral values\n  app_name = \"my-application\"\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Testing Your Migration\n\nAfter upgrading to Terraform v1.10.0, follow these validation steps:\n\n### 1. Validate Backend Configuration\n\n```bash\nterraform init -reconfigure\n```\n\nIf the S3 backend migration was incomplete, you will see errors like:\n```\nError: Unsupported argument\n  An argument named \"role_arn\" is not expected here.\n```\n\n### 2. Validate Configuration Syntax\n\n```bash\nterraform validate\n```\n\nThis will catch:\n- `moved` block reserved keyword conflicts\n- Ephemeral value used in non-ephemeral context\n- Invalid ephemeral resource lifecycle arguments\n\n### 3. Review Plan Output for Sensitive Value Changes\n\n```bash\nterraform plan\n```\n\nCompare the plan output to what you saw in v1.9.0. If outputs that previously showed plain values now show `(sensitive value)`, determine whether this is expected (the value genuinely is sensitive) or whether you need to use `nonsensitive()`.\n\n### 4. Check for Moved Block Errors\n\nIf you have `moved` blocks, verify that the plan shows resource moves (not destroys and creates):\n\n```\n# The following resources are moved:\n  # aws_instance.old (from resource.local.old)\n  # aws_instance.new (to resource.local.new)\n```\n\nIf you see unexpected destroy/create pairs instead of moves, review the `moved` block addresses for keyword conflicts.\n\n### 5. Test in a Non-Production Environment First\n\nBefore upgrading production environments, run through the upgrade process in a staging or development environment. Pay particular attention to:\n- State locking behavior (especially if enabling `use_lockfile`)\n- Sensitive value changes in plan output\n- Any CI/CD pipeline scripts that parse `terraform plan` or `terraform output`\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\nIf you need to roll back from v1.10.0 to v1.9.0, follow these steps:\n\n### Before the Upgrade (Prevention)\n\n1. **Tag or snapshot the current state** in your S3 bucket before upgrading. If you use S3 versioning (highly recommended), note the current version ID.\n\n2. **Retain your original configuration files** \u2014 do not commit the upgraded configurations until you have validated the upgrade in your environment.\n\n### Rolling Back the Terraform Binary\n\n1. **Reinstall Terraform v1.9.0** using your preferred installation method (e.g., `tfenv`, direct binary download, package manager).\n\n2. **Revert configuration changes** made during the upgrade:\n   - Restore root-level S3 backend IAM attributes if you had migrated to `assume_role` block (temporarily re-add them)\n   - Remove `resource.` prefix from `moved` block addresses if you had added them\n   - Remove ephemeral resources, variables, and outputs (they were not in v1.9.0)\n\n3. **Run `terraform init`** to re-initialize with the reverted configuration.\n\n4. **Run `terraform plan`** to confirm the plan is clean (no unexpected changes).\n\n### State Compatibility\n\nThe Terraform state format is backward compatible between v1.9.0 and v1.10.0. Rolling back the Terraform binary version **does not require state migration**. The state file written by v1.10.0 can be read by v1.9.0.\n\n> **Exception**: If you used any new v1.10.0 ephemeral resource features, those resources are not stored in state (by design), so there is no state compatibility concern for those.\n\n### S3 Native Locking Rollback\n\nIf you enabled `use_lockfile = true` and need to roll back:\n\n1. Remove `use_lockfile = true` from your backend configuration\n2. Check that no `.tflock` files are left in S3 (they should not be present if all operations completed cleanly, but orphaned lock files from interrupted runs may need to be manually deleted)\n3. Run `terraform init -reconfigure` to update the backend configuration\n\n### Known Rollback Risks\n\n- **`moved` block changes**: If you added `resource.` prefixes to `moved` blocks and then roll back to v1.9.0, those prefixes are accepted by v1.9.0 as well, so the rollback is safe.\n- **`assume_role` block migration**: If you have already migrated to the `assume_role` block syntax and need to re-add root-level attributes temporarily, you will see deprecation warnings in v1.9.0 but the configuration will work.\n- **Sensitive value changes**: Rolling back the binary does not change how existing sensitive values in state are treated. However, outputs that are now correctly marked as sensitive in v1.10.0 will revert to potentially leaking in v1.9.0.\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n- [Terraform v1.10 Changelog](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [S3 Backend Configuration Reference](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/backend/s3)\n- [Ephemeral Resources Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/resources/ephemeral)\n- [Ephemeral Input Variables](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/values/variables#exclude-values-from-state)\n- [Ephemeral Outputs](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/values/outputs#ephemeral-avoid-storing-values-in-state-or-plan-files)\n- [nonsensitive() Function](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/functions/nonsensitive)\n- [ephemeralasnull() Function](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/functions/ephemeralasnull)\n- [moved Block Reference](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/moved)\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"

{
  "content": "# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 was released on November 27, 2024. It is a minor release in the stable Terraform v1.0 series and honors the [Terraform v1.0 Compatibility Promises](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1-compatibility-promises).\n\nThis release introduces several breaking changes and significant new features:\n\n- **Breaking**: Removed deprecated root-level IAM role assumption attributes from the S3 backend \u2014 must migrate to `assume_role` block syntax\n- **Breaking**: `moved` blocks now enforce reserved keyword restrictions on resource type names \u2014 may require adding `resource.` prefix\n- **Behavioral change**: Conditional expressions now preserve sensitive marks in all branches \u2014 previously some marks were silently dropped\n- **New feature**: Ephemeral resources, ephemeral input variables, and ephemeral outputs \u2014 a mechanism to avoid persisting sensitive values to state\n- **New feature**: S3 native state locking (`use_lockfile`) as an experimental opt-in alternative to DynamoDB locking\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. S3 Backend: Removal of Deprecated Root-Level IAM Role Assumption Attributes\n\n#### What Changed and Why\n\nIn v1.9.0, the following root-level attributes in the S3 backend were deprecated with replacements inside an `assume_role` block. In **v1.10.0, these deprecated attributes have been completely removed**. Any S3 backend configuration still using them will fail with an error at `terraform init`.\n\n| Removed Attribute | Replacement Inside `assume_role` Block |\n|---|---|\n| `role_arn` | `assume_role.role_arn` |\n| `session_name` | `assume_role.session_name` |\n| `external_id` | `assume_role.external_id` |\n| `assume_role_duration_seconds` | `assume_role.duration` |\n| `assume_role_policy` | `assume_role.policy` |\n| `assume_role_policy_arns` | `assume_role.policy_arns` |\n| `assume_role_tags` | `assume_role.tags` |\n| `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` | `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys` |\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0 \u2014 deprecated but functional)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket       = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key          = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region       = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # These root-level attributes are REMOVED in v1.10.0\n    role_arn                     = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n    session_name                 = \"terraform-session\"\n    external_id                  = \"my-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds = 3600\n    assume_role_policy           = jsonencode({ ... })\n    assume_role_policy_arns      = [\"arn:aws:iam::aws:policy/ReadOnlyAccess\"]\n    assume_role_tags = {\n      Environment = \"production\"\n    }\n    assume_role_transitive_tag_keys = [\"Environment\"]\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0 \u2014 required syntax)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    assume_role = {\n      role_arn     = \"arn:aws:iam::123456789012:role/TerraformRole\"\n      session_name = \"terraform-session\"\n      external_id  = \"my-external-id\"\n      duration     = \"1h\"\n      policy       = jsonencode({ ... })\n      policy_arns  = [\"arn:aws:iam::aws:policy/ReadOnlyAccess\"]\n      tags = {\n        Environment = \"production\"\n      }\n      transitive_tag_keys = [\"Environment\"]\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### Step-by-Step Migration Instructions\n\n1. **Audit all S3 backend configurations** \u2014 search your codebase for `backend \"s3\"` blocks and identify any that use the root-level deprecated attributes:\n\n   ```bash\n   grep -rn \"role_arn\\|session_name\\|external_id\\|assume_role_duration_seconds\\|assume_role_policy\\|assume_role_tags\\|assume_role_transitive_tag_keys\" \\\n     --include=\"*.tf\" --include=\"*.tfvars\" .\n   ```\n\n   Also check any partial backend configuration files (commonly passed with `-backend-config`).\n\n2. **Refactor each backend block** \u2014 move all role assumption attributes inside an `assume_role = { ... }` block:\n\n   - `role_arn` \u2192 `assume_role.role_arn` (note: now **required** within the block if assuming a role)\n   - `session_name` \u2192 `assume_role.session_name`\n   - `external_id` \u2192 `assume_role.external_id`\n   - `assume_role_duration_seconds` (integer, seconds) \u2192 `assume_role.duration` (string, e.g., `\"1h30m\"`)\n   - `assume_role_policy` \u2192 `assume_role.policy`\n   - `assume_role_policy_arns` \u2192 `assume_role.policy_arns`\n   - `assume_role_tags` \u2192 `assume_role.tags`\n   - `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` \u2192 `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys`\n\n   > **Note on `duration` format**: The old `assume_role_duration_seconds` accepted an integer (e.g., `3600`). The new `assume_role.duration` accepts a duration string (e.g., `\"1h\"`, `\"90m\"`, `\"1h30m\"`). Valid range is 15 minutes (`15m`) to 12 hours (`12h`).\n\n3. **Run `terraform init`** on each updated backend configuration to validate the new syntax.\n\n4. **Check partial backend config files** \u2014 if you use `-backend-config=backend.hcl` or `-backend-config=\"key=value\"` flags, update those as well.\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- The `assume_role` value is a **block** (or map), not a string. Use `assume_role = { ... }`, not `assume_role = \"...\"`.\n- If you only used `role_arn` at the root level, you now need `assume_role = { role_arn = \"...\" }`.\n- Multiple `assume_role` blocks are supported \u2014 roles are assumed in order \u2014 but this was not available with the old root-level attributes.\n- The `duration` format changed from seconds (integer) to a duration string. `3600` seconds becomes `\"1h\"`.\n\n---\n\n### 2. S3 Backend: New S3 Native State Locking\n\n#### What Changed and Why\n\nThe S3 backend gained a new experimental opt-in feature: **S3-native state locking** using `.tflock` files. This is not a breaking change by itself since it is opt-in, but it has operational implications worth understanding before upgrading.\n\nWhen `use_lockfile = true` is set, Terraform creates a lock file alongside the state file in S3 (same path, with a `.tflock` extension). When both `use_lockfile` and `dynamodb_table` are configured, **both locking mechanisms must succeed** before operations proceed.\n\n> **Important**: In a future minor version of Terraform, the DynamoDB locking mechanism and its associated arguments will be deprecated. The `use_lockfile` attribute will move out of experimental status at that time.\n\n#### Enabling S3 Native Locking (Optional)\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket       = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key          = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region       = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Opt-in to experimental S3-native locking\n    use_lockfile = true\n\n    # Can be used alongside DynamoDB locking (both must succeed)\n    dynamodb_table = \"terraform-state-locks\"\n  }\n}\n```\n\n#### IAM Permission Updates Required\n\nIf you enable `use_lockfile = true`, ensure the IAM principal running Terraform has permissions to read, write, and delete the lock file in S3:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"Version\": \"2012-10-17\",\n  \"Statement\": [\n    {\n      \"Effect\": \"Allow\",\n      \"Action\": [\"s3:GetObject\", \"s3:PutObject\", \"s3:DeleteObject\"],\n      \"Resource\": \"arn:aws:s3:::my-bucket/path/to/state.tflock\"\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\nFor workspace-aware configurations, the lock file path follows the workspace state path pattern with `.tflock` appended.\n\n---\n\n### 3. `moved` Blocks: Reserved Keyword Restriction on Resource Type Names\n\n#### What Changed and Why\n\nIn v1.10.0, `moved` block resource address parsing now **rejects resource type names that conflict with reserved keywords** (`local`, `each`, `self`, `count`, `module`, `path`, `terraform`, `var`, and other top-level block types).\n\nPreviously, a `moved` block referencing a resource whose type name happened to match a keyword (e.g., `resource \"local\" \"my_file\" { ... }`) would be parsed without error but could produce incorrect behavior. Now Terraform will report an error and require you to prepend `resource.` to the address to disambiguate.\n\n#### Affected Configurations\n\nThis affects `moved` blocks where the resource type name collides with a Terraform keyword or top-level block type. Common examples include:\n\n- `local` (conflicts with `local` values)\n- `count` (conflicts with `count` meta-argument)\n- `each` (conflicts with `each` in for_each)\n- `self` (conflicts with `self` reference)\n- `module` (conflicts with `module` block)\n- `var` (conflicts with `var` reference)\n- `path` (conflicts with `path` object)\n- `terraform` (conflicts with `terraform` block)\n- `data` (conflicts with `data` sources)\n- `check` (conflicts with `check` block)\n\n#### Before (v1.9.0 \u2014 ambiguous but accepted)\n\n```hcl\n# Resource with a type name matching a keyword\nresource \"local\" \"config\" {\n  filename = \"/tmp/config.txt\"\n  content  = \"hello\"\n}\n\n# Old moved block \u2014 ambiguous in v1.9.0, error in v1.10.0\nmoved {\n  from = local.config\n  to   = local.config_v2\n}\n```\n\n#### After (v1.10.0 \u2014 required syntax)\n\n```hcl\nresource \"local\" \"config\" {\n  filename = \"/tmp/config.txt\"\n  content  = \"hello\"\n}\n\n# Explicit resource. prefix required when type name conflicts with keywords\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.config\n  to   = resource.local.config_v2\n}\n```\n\n#### Step-by-Step Migration Instructions\n\n1. **Find all `moved` blocks** in your configuration:\n\n   ```bash\n   grep -rn \"^moved {\" --include=\"*.tf\" .\n   ```\n\n2. **Check both `from` and `to` addresses** in each `moved` block. For each address, identify whether the first component (the resource type name) matches any of the following reserved keywords:\n\n   `local`, `each`, `self`, `count`, `module`, `var`, `path`, `terraform`, `data`, `check`, `resource`\n\n3. **Add the `resource.` prefix** to any address where the resource type name conflicts with a keyword:\n\n   ```hcl\n   # BEFORE\n   moved {\n     from = local.old_name\n     to   = local.new_name\n   }\n\n   # AFTER\n   moved {\n     from = resource.local.old_name\n     to   = resource.local.new_name\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Run `terraform validate`** to confirm no moved block errors remain.\n\n5. **Run `terraform plan`** to verify the moved blocks are interpreted correctly (the plan should show moves, not destroys+creates).\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- Only addresses in `moved` blocks are affected. Normal resource references (in `resource`, `data`, `locals`, etc.) are unaffected.\n- The `resource.` prefix is only required when the type name **conflicts with a keyword**. Resources with ordinary type names (e.g., `aws_instance`, `azurerm_resource_group`) do not require the prefix.\n- Both `from` and `to` addresses may independently require the prefix \u2014 check both.\n- If you have modules with `moved` blocks, the inner module addresses also need to be checked.\n\n---\n\n## Behavioral Changes\n\n### 4. Sensitive Value Handling in Conditional Expressions\n\n#### What Changed and Why\n\nIn v1.10.0, a bug was fixed in how HCL evaluates conditional expressions and `for` expressions: **sensitive marks (and other value marks) are now consistently propagated across all branches** of an expression, even when some branches contain unknown values.\n\nPreviously, certain combinations of unknown values in conditional expressions could cause marks to be silently dropped. This meant a value that should have been treated as sensitive was not, potentially exposing it in plan output or in state without warning.\n\nThe fix ensures that if any value in a conditional expression (condition, true branch, or false branch) carries a sensitive mark, that mark is preserved in the result. This is more correct behavior and improves security, but it means **configurations that previously produced non-sensitive outputs may now produce sensitive outputs**.\n\nAdditionally, the `issensitive()` function could previously incorrectly assert that an unknown value was not sensitive during plan, but later become sensitive during apply, causing plan/apply mismatches. This has also been fixed.\n\n#### Scenarios Where You May See Changes\n\n**Scenario 1: Conditional with a sensitive condition**\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"secret\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\n# In v1.9.0: this may produce a non-sensitive value in some cases\n# In v1.10.0: result is always sensitive because secret is sensitive\noutput \"result\" {\n  value = var.secret == \"expected\" ? \"yes\" : \"no\"\n}\n```\n\n**Scenario 2: Conditional with a sensitive branch value**\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"use_secret\" {\n  type    = bool\n  default = false\n}\n\nvariable \"secret_value\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\n# In v1.9.0: if use_secret is unknown at plan time, marks could be lost\n# In v1.10.0: result is always sensitive because secret_value is sensitive\noutput \"chosen_value\" {\n  value = var.use_secret ? var.secret_value : \"public-default\"\n}\n```\n\n**Scenario 3: For expression with sensitive values**\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"secrets\" {\n  type      = list(string)\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\n# In v1.10.0: transformed values retain the sensitive mark\nlocals {\n  processed = [for s in var.secrets : upper(s)]\n}\n```\n\n#### Impact Assessment\n\nThis change **does not alter the underlying values** \u2014 it only changes whether Terraform marks them as sensitive. The practical effects are:\n\n- Plan output may now show `(sensitive value)` where it previously showed the actual value\n- Outputs that previously appeared in the output table may now be suppressed as sensitive\n- `issensitive()` function results will be more accurate (fewer false negatives during plan)\n\n#### How to Use `nonsensitive()` to Override When Needed\n\nIf you have a derivation from a sensitive value that you know is safe to expose (because the sensitive information has been removed in the transformation), you can use the `nonsensitive()` function to explicitly override Terraform's conservative behavior:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\n# This is derived from a sensitive value but only shows length \u2014 safe to expose\noutput \"password_length\" {\n  # nonsensitive() tells Terraform this derived value is not sensitive\n  value = nonsensitive(length(var.db_password))\n}\n\n# A hash of a password \u2014 whether this is safe depends on your threat model\noutput \"password_hash\" {\n  value = nonsensitive(sha256(var.db_password))\n}\n```\n\n> **Warning**: Only use `nonsensitive()` when you are certain the derived value does not expose sensitive information. Using it incorrectly will cause sensitive data to appear in plain text in Terraform output and state files. Add a comment explaining why the usage is safe.\n\n#### Step-by-Step Migration Instructions\n\n1. **Run `terraform plan`** after upgrading to identify any new sensitive value warnings or output changes.\n\n2. **Review outputs** that previously showed plain values but now show `(sensitive value)`. Determine whether:\n   - The output _should_ be sensitive (in which case no action is needed \u2014 this is a security improvement), or\n   - The output genuinely does not contain sensitive information (in which case use `nonsensitive()`)\n\n3. **Update CI/CD pipelines** that parse plan output \u2014 if your automation reads specific output values from `terraform output`, ensure it handles `(sensitive value)` appropriately.\n\n4. **Review `issensitive()` usage** \u2014 if you used `issensitive()` in validation conditions or locals to conditionally handle values, test that the corrected behavior meets your expectations.\n\n#### Common Pitfalls\n\n- Do not add `nonsensitive()` indiscriminately to silence warnings. Each usage requires careful consideration of whether it is actually safe.\n- The change improves correctness \u2014 if you were relying on marks being dropped (e.g., to output a sensitive value without marking it), that was a bug and you should redesign that part of your configuration.\n- `sensitive` and `ephemeral` are separate concepts \u2014 `sensitive` controls display and state storage, while `ephemeral` (new in v1.10.0) prevents state storage entirely. See the Ephemeral Values section for details.\n\n---\n\n## New Features with Migration Impact\n\n### 5. Ephemeral Resources and Values\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces a new concept of **ephemeral values**: data that is available during Terraform operations but is **never written to state or plan files**. This is a fundamentally different mechanism from `sensitive`, which only suppresses display of values that are still stored in state.\n\n> **Note**: Ephemeral resources, variables, and outputs are in public beta in v1.10.0. Workflows may change in future versions.\n\n#### Ephemeral Resources\n\nA new `ephemeral` block type defines resources that are read fresh during each operation phase and never stored in state:\n\n```hcl\nephemeral \"aws_secretsmanager_secret_version\" \"db_creds\" {\n  secret_id = data.aws_db_instance.example.master_user_secret[0].secret_arn\n}\n\nlocals {\n  credentials = jsondecode(ephemeral.aws_secretsmanager_secret_version.db_creds.secret_string)\n}\n\nprovider \"postgresql\" {\n  host     = data.aws_db_instance.example.address\n  username = local.credentials[\"username\"]\n  password = local.credentials[\"password\"]\n}\n```\n\n**Ephemeral resource lifecycle:**\n1. **Open**: Terraform fetches the resource (e.g., obtains a Vault lease)\n2. **Renew** (if needed): Terraform keeps the resource alive if the operation is long-running\n3. **Close**: Terraform releases the resource when it is no longer needed (e.g., ends the Vault lease)\n\n**Supported meta-arguments for ephemeral resources:**\n- `depends_on`\n- `count`\n- `for_each`\n- `provider`\n- `lifecycle`\n\n**Not supported:** `provisioner` meta-argument.\n\n#### Ephemeral Input Variables\n\nInput variables can be marked as ephemeral to prevent their values from being written to state or plan files:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"session_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n```\n\nUnlike `sensitive`, which still stores values in state (just marking them as sensitive), `ephemeral = true` means the value is **never persisted**. This is appropriate for short-lived tokens, one-time passwords, or credentials that rotate frequently.\n\n**Valid contexts for ephemeral variables:**\n- Other ephemeral variables\n- Local values (which become implicitly ephemeral)\n- Ephemeral resources\n- Ephemeral outputs\n- Provider configuration blocks\n- `provisioner` and `connection` blocks\n\n#### Ephemeral Outputs\n\nOutputs in child modules can be marked ephemeral to pass ephemeral values between modules without persisting them:\n\n```hcl\n# modules/secrets/main.tf\noutput \"api_key\" {\n  value       = ephemeral.vault_kv_secret.app.data[\"api_key\"]\n  ephemeral   = true\n  description = \"Temporary API key for the application.\"\n}\n```\n\n> **Restriction**: Ephemeral outputs cannot be set in the **root module**. They are only supported in child modules.\n\n#### The `ephemeralasnull` Function\n\nA new built-in function `ephemeralasnull` converts ephemeral values to `null`, enabling outputs of mixed ephemeral/non-ephemeral objects:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"session_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\nvariable \"environment\" {\n  type    = string\n  default = \"production\"\n}\n\nlocals {\n  config = {\n    env   = var.environment\n    token = var.session_token\n  }\n  # implicitly ephemeral because it contains an ephemeral value\n}\n\noutput \"config_summary\" {\n  # ephemeralasnull replaces ephemeral values with null,\n  # allowing non-ephemeral values to be output\n  value = ephemeralasnull(local.config)\n}\n# Output: { \"env\" = \"production\", \"token\" = null }\n```\n\n#### Migrating from `sensitive` to `ephemeral` for Secret Handling\n\nIf your current configurations use `sensitive` purely to prevent secrets from appearing in state, consider migrating to `ephemeral` for stronger guarantees:\n\n| Mechanism | Appears in State | Displayed in UI | Use Case |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `sensitive = true` | Yes (encrypted at rest if backend supports it) | Suppressed | Data that must be preserved across runs |\n| `ephemeral = true` | **No** | Not displayed | Temporary credentials, tokens, one-time values |\n\n**Before (v1.9.0 and earlier \u2014 sensitive approach):**\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nresource \"aws_db_instance\" \"main\" {\n  password = var.db_password\n  # password is stored in state (sensitive but present)\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0 \u2014 ephemeral approach for maximum privacy):**\n\n```hcl\nephemeral \"aws_secretsmanager_secret_version\" \"db_pass\" {\n  secret_id = aws_secretsmanager_secret.db_password.id\n}\n\nresource \"aws_db_instance\" \"main\" {\n  password = ephemeral.aws_secretsmanager_secret_version.db_pass.secret_string\n  # password is never written to state\n}\n```\n\n> **Note**: Not all resource arguments accept ephemeral values. Provider support is required. Check the relevant provider's documentation for which arguments support ephemeral values.\n\n#### Implicit Ephemeral Propagation\n\nEphemeral values propagate implicitly through local values and expressions:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"api_token\" {\n  type      = string\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\nlocals {\n  # Implicitly ephemeral \u2014 inherits from var.api_token\n  auth_header = \"Bearer ${var.api_token}\"\n\n  # Not ephemeral \u2014 does not reference ephemeral values\n  app_name = \"my-application\"\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Testing Your Migration\n\nAfter upgrading to Terraform v1.10.0, follow these validation steps:\n\n### 1. Validate Backend Configuration\n\n```bash\nterraform init -reconfigure\n```\n\nIf the S3 backend migration was incomplete, you will see errors like:\n```\nError: Unsupported argument\n  An argument named \"role_arn\" is not expected here.\n```\n\n### 2. Validate Configuration Syntax\n\n```bash\nterraform validate\n```\n\nThis will catch:\n- `moved` block reserved keyword conflicts\n- Ephemeral value used in non-ephemeral context\n- Invalid ephemeral resource lifecycle arguments\n\n### 3. Review Plan Output for Sensitive Value Changes\n\n```bash\nterraform plan\n```\n\nCompare the plan output to what you saw in v1.9.0. If outputs that previously showed plain values now show `(sensitive value)`, determine whether this is expected (the value genuinely is sensitive) or whether you need to use `nonsensitive()`.\n\n### 4. Check for Moved Block Errors\n\nIf you have `moved` blocks, verify that the plan shows resource moves (not destroys and creates):\n\n```\n# The following resources are moved:\n  # aws_instance.old (from resource.local.old)\n  # aws_instance.new (to resource.local.new)\n```\n\nIf you see unexpected destroy/create pairs instead of moves, review the `moved` block addresses for keyword conflicts.\n\n### 5. Test in a Non-Production Environment First\n\nBefore upgrading production environments, run through the upgrade process in a staging or development environment. Pay particular attention to:\n- State locking behavior (especially if enabling `use_lockfile`)\n- Sensitive value changes in plan output\n- Any CI/CD pipeline scripts that parse `terraform plan` or `terraform output`\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\nIf you need to roll back from v1.10.0 to v1.9.0, follow these steps:\n\n### Before the Upgrade (Prevention)\n\n1. **Tag or snapshot the current state** in your S3 bucket before upgrading. If you use S3 versioning (highly recommended), note the current version ID.\n\n2. **Retain your original configuration files** \u2014 do not commit the upgraded configurations until you have validated the upgrade in your environment.\n\n### Rolling Back the Terraform Binary\n\n1. **Reinstall Terraform v1.9.0** using your preferred installation method (e.g., `tfenv`, direct binary download, package manager).\n\n2. **Revert configuration changes** made during the upgrade:\n   - Restore root-level S3 backend IAM attributes if you had migrated to `assume_role` block (temporarily re-add them)\n   - Remove `resource.` prefix from `moved` block addresses if you had added them\n   - Remove ephemeral resources, variables, and outputs (they were not in v1.9.0)\n\n3. **Run `terraform init`** to re-initialize with the reverted configuration.\n\n4. **Run `terraform plan`** to confirm the plan is clean (no unexpected changes).\n\n### State Compatibility\n\nThe Terraform state format is backward compatible between v1.9.0 and v1.10.0. Rolling back the Terraform binary version **does not require state migration**. The state file written by v1.10.0 can be read by v1.9.0.\n\n> **Exception**: If you used any new v1.10.0 ephemeral resource features, those resources are not stored in state (by design), so there is no state compatibility concern for those.\n\n### S3 Native Locking Rollback\n\nIf you enabled `use_lockfile = true` and need to roll back:\n\n1. Remove `use_lockfile = true` from your backend configuration\n2. Check that no `.tflock` files are left in S3 (they should not be present if all operations completed cleanly, but orphaned lock files from interrupted runs may need to be manually deleted)\n3. Run `terraform init -reconfigure` to update the backend configuration\n\n### Known Rollback Risks\n\n- **`moved` block changes**: If you added `resource.` prefixes to `moved` blocks and then roll back to v1.9.0, those prefixes are accepted by v1.9.0 as well, so the rollback is safe.\n- **`assume_role` block migration**: If you have already migrated to the `assume_role` block syntax and need to re-add root-level attributes temporarily, you will see deprecation warnings in v1.9.0 but the configuration will work.\n- **Sensitive value changes**: Rolling back the binary does not change how existing sensitive values in state are treated. However, outputs that are now correctly marked as sensitive in v1.10.0 will revert to potentially leaking in v1.9.0.\n\n---\n\n## Additional Resources\n\n- [Terraform v1.10 Changelog](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.10/CHANGELOG.md)\n- [S3 Backend Configuration Reference](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/backend/s3)\n- [Ephemeral Resources Documentation](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/resources/ephemeral)\n- [Ephemeral Input Variables](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/values/variables#exclude-values-from-state)\n- [Ephemeral Outputs](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/values/outputs#ephemeral-avoid-storing-values-in-state-or-plan-files)\n- [nonsensitive() Function](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/functions/nonsensitive)\n- [ephemeralasnull() Function](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/functions/ephemeralasnull)\n- [moved Block Reference](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/moved)\n",

1. WRITE /workspace/documentation.md
# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide

## Overview

Terraform v1.10.0 was released on November 27, 2024. It is a minor release in the stable Terraform v1.0 series and honors the [Terraform v1.0 Compatibility Promises](https://developer.hashicorp.com/terraform/language/v1-compatibility-promises).

This release introduces several breaking changes and significant new features:

- **Breaking**: Removed deprecated root-level IAM role assumption attributes from the S3 backend — must migrate to `assume_role` block syntax
- **Breaking**: `moved` blocks now enforce reserved keyword restrictions on resource type names — may require adding `resource.` prefix
- **Behavioral change**: Conditional expressions now preserve sensitive marks in all branches — previously some marks were silently dropped
- **New feature**: Ephemeral resources, ephemeral input variables, and ephemeral outputs — a mechanism to avoid persisting sensitive values to state
- **New feature**: S3 native state locking (`use_lockfile`) as an experimental opt-in alternative to DynamoDB locking

---

## Breaking Changes

### 1. S3 Backend: Removal of Deprecated Root-Level IAM Role Assumption Attributes

#### What Changed and Why

In v1.9.0, the following root-level attributes in the S3 backend were deprecated with replacements inside an `assume_role` block. In **v1.10.0, these deprecated attributes have been completely removed**. Any S3 backend configuration still using them will fail with an error at `terraform init`.

| Removed Attribute | Replacement Inside `assume_role` Block |
|---|---|
| `role_arn` | `assume_role.role_arn` |
| `session_name` | `assume_role.session_name` |
| `external_id` | `assume_role.external_id` |
| `assume_role_duration_seconds` | `assume_role.duration` |
| `assume_role_policy` | `as
... (truncated)
